      <p><b>Dominica</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-pronunciation_guardian_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation_guardian-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pronunciation_virtual_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation_virtual-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-Cambridge_Dictionary_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cambridge_Dictionary-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kalinago_language" title="Kalinago language">Kalinago language</a>: <i lang="car" title="Galibi Carib-language text">Wai‘tu kubuli</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Dominique</i>; <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Creole_French" title="Dominican Creole French">Dominican Creole French</a>: <i>Dominik</i>), officially the <b>Commonwealth of Dominica</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-English_constitution_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_constitution-13">[13]</a></sup> The capital, <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a>, is located on the western side of the island. It is geographically situated as part of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> chain in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> archipelago in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. The island is located near <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> to the northwest and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> to the south-southeast. Its area is 750&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (290&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and the highest point is <a href="/wiki/Morne_Diablotins" title="Morne Diablotins">Morne Diablotins</a>, at 1,447&nbsp;m (4,747&nbsp;ft) in elevation. The population was 71,293 at the 2011 census.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_census_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_census-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The island was settled by the <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> arriving from South America in the 5th century. The <a href="/wiki/Kalinago" title="Kalinago">Kalinago</a> displaced the Arawak by the 15th century. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a> is said to have passed the island on Sunday, 3 November 1493. It was later colonised by Europeans, predominantly by the French from the 1690s to 1763. The French imported enslaved people from West Africa to Dominica to work on coffee plantations. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> took possession in 1763 after the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, and it gradually established English as its official language. The island gained independence as a republic in 1978. </p>
      <p>Dominica has been nicknamed the "Nature Isle of the Caribbean" for its natural environment.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> It is the youngest island in the Lesser Antilles, and in fact it is still being formed by <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Geothermal (geology)">geothermal</a>-<a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> activity, as evidenced by the world's second-largest <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot spring</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Boiling_Lake" title="Boiling Lake">Boiling Lake</a>. The island has lush mountainous <a href="/wiki/Rainforests" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainforests">rainforests</a>, and it is the home of many rare plants, animals, and bird species. There are <a href="/wiki/Xeric" class="mw-redirect" title="Xeric">xeric</a> areas in some of the western coastal regions, but heavy rainfall occurs inland. The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_amazon" title="Imperial amazon">sisserou parrot</a>, also known as the imperial amazon and found only on Dominica, is the island's national bird and featured on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Dominica" title="Flag of Dominica">national flag</a>, which is one of only two national flags containing the colour purple (the other being <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Dominica's name is locally pronounced with emphasis on the third syllable,<sup id="cite_ref-pronunciation_guardian_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation_guardian-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pronunciation_virtual_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation_virtual-10">[10]</a></sup> following the Spanish pronunciation of its name<sup id="cite_ref-pronunciation_stuff_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation_stuff-16">[16]</a></sup> given to it by Christopher Columbus. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dominica" title="History of Dominica">History of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geologic_history">Geologic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geologic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica first emerged from the sea during the <a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> era approximately 26 million years ago, making it one of the last Caribbean islands to be formed by <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic activity</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period_and_early_European_contact">Pre-colonial period and early European contact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period and early European contact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica's precolonial indigenous inhabitants were the <a href="/wiki/Island_Carib" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Carib">Island Carib</a> people, who are thought to have driven out the previous <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> The Caribs called the island <i>Wai‘tu kubuli</i>, which means "Tall is her body."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, sailing for <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, named the island as Dominica, after the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> term <i>dies Dominica</i> for <a href="/wiki/Sunday" title="Sunday">Sunday</a>, the day on which the Spanish first saw it in November 1493.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Some Spanish colonisers settled here. But, as European explorers and settlers entered the region, indigenous refugees from surrounding islands settled Dominica and pushed out the Spanish settlers. The Spanish instead settled other areas that were easier to control and had more natural resources. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colony">French colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Spain had little success in colonising Dominica. In 1632, the French <a href="/wiki/Compagnie_des_%C3%8Eles_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique" class="mw-redirect" title="Compagnie des Îles de l'Amérique">Compagnie des Îles de l'Amérique</a> claimed it and other <i>"Petites Antilles"</i> for <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>, but no physical occupation took place.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Between 1642 and 1650, French missionary <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Breton" title="Raymond Breton">Raymond Breton</a> became the first regular European visitor to the island. </p>
      <p>In 1660, the French and English agreed that Dominica and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent (island)">St. Vincent</a> should not be settled, but instead left to the Carib as neutral territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> But its natural resources attracted expeditions of English and French foresters, who began harvesting timber.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1690, the French established their first permanent settlements. French woodcutters from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> began to set up timber camps to supply the French islands with wood, and they gradually became permanent settlers. They brought the first enslaved Africans from West Africa to <i>Dominique</i>, as they called it in French. </p>
      <p>In 1715, a revolt of "poor white" smallholders in the north of Martinique, known as La Gaoulé,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> caused settlers to migrate to southern Dominique, where they set up <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholdings</a>. Meanwhile, French families and others from Guadeloupe settled in the north. In 1727, the first French commander, <a href="/w/index.php?title=M._Le_Grand&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="M. Le Grand (page does not exist)">M. Le Grand</a>, took charge of the island with a basic French government. Dominique formally became a <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> of France, and the island was divided into districts or "quarters".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The French had already developed plantation agriculture on Martinique and Guadeloupe, where they cultivated <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> with enslaved African workers. In Dominique they gradually developed coffee plantations. They imported so many African <a href="/wiki/Slaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Slaves">slaves</a> to fill the labour demands that the population became predominantly African in ethnicity. </p>
      <p>In 1761, during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> in Europe, a <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Dominica" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Dominica">British expedition against Dominica</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Rollo,_5th_Lord_Rollo" title="Andrew Rollo, 5th Lord Rollo">Andrew Rollo</a> conquered the island, along with several other Caribbean islands. In 1763, France had lost the war and ceded the island to Great Britain under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> The same year, the British established a <a href="/wiki/Legislative_assembly" title="Legislative assembly">legislative assembly</a>, with only European colonists represented. French remained the official language, but <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a>, which had developed from it, was spoken by most of the population. </p>
      <p>In 1778 the French, with the active co-operation of the population, began the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Dominica_(1778)" title="Invasion of Dominica (1778)">re-capture of Dominica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> This was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris (1783)</a>, which returned the island to British control. But the island population, especially the class of <a href="/wiki/Gens_de_couleur" class="mw-redirect" title="Gens de couleur">free people of color</a>, resisted British restrictions. The British retained control through French invasions in 1795 and 1805,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> the first taking place during the period of the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a>, which gained the independence of Haiti (formerly Saint-Domingue, France's richest Caribbean colony). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colony">British colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: British colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market,_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market%2C_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3520" data-file-height="2551"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Agostino_Brunias_-_Linen_Market,_Dominica_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A linen market in 1770s Dominica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Great Britain established a small colony in 1805. It used Dominica as part of the <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a>, by which slaves were imported and sold as labour in the islands as part of a trade that included producing and shipping sugar and coffee as commodity crops to Europe. The best documented slave plantation on the island is Hillsborough Estate, which had 71 male and 68 female slaves. The <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Bank_Mill" title="Quarry Bank Mill">Greg</a> family were notable: Thomas Hodgson, a brother-in-law, owned a slave ship, and Thomas Greg and his son John Greg were part-owners of <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar plantation">sugar plantations</a> on Dominica. In January 1814, 20 slaves absconded from Hillsborough. They were recorded as recaptured and punished with 100 lashes applied to the males and 50 for the females. The slaves reportedly said that one of their people had died in the plantation hospital, and they believed he had been poisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1831, reflecting a liberalisation of official British racial attitudes, the Brown Privilege Bill<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> conferred political and social rights on <a href="/wiki/Free_black" class="mw-redirect" title="Free black">free blacks</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_colour" class="mw-redirect" title="Free people of colour">free people of colour</a>, who generally were of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed race">mixed race</a>, with African and European ancestry). With the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">Slavery Abolition Act of 1833</a>, Britain ended the institution of slavery throughout <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">its empire</a>, except in India.<sup id="cite_ref-SectionLXIV_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SectionLXIV-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With freedom came enfranchisement. In 1835, the first three men of African descent were elected to the legislative assembly of Dominica. Many slaves from the neighbouring French colonial islands of Guadeloupe and Martinique fled to Dominica. In 1838, Dominica became the first colony of the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> to have an elected legislature controlled by an ethnic African majority. Most of these legislators had been free people of colour and smallholders or merchants before the abolition of slavery. Their economic and social views were different from the interests of the small, wealthy English <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">planter</a> class. Reacting to a perceived threat to their power, the planters lobbied for more direct British rule.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1865, after much agitation and tension, the colonial office replaced the elective assembly with one made up of one-half members who were elected and one-half who were appointed. Planters, who were allied with colonial administrators, outmanoeuvred the elected legislators on many occasions. In 1871, Dominica became part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>. The political power of the ethnic African population progressively eroded. <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> government was re-established in 1896. All political rights were curtailed for people of colour and blacks, who were the overwhelming majority of the population. Development aid, offered as compensation for disfranchisement, resulted in negligible improvements in conditions for most ethnic Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dominica_stamps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dominica_stamps.jpg/220px-Dominica_stamps.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dominica_stamps.jpg/330px-Dominica_stamps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dominica_stamps.jpg/440px-Dominica_stamps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5243" data-file-height="3349"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dominica_stamps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dominica stamps with portraits of <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, many Dominicans, mainly the sons of small farmers, volunteered to fight in Europe for the British Empire. After the war, an upsurge of political consciousness throughout the Caribbean led to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_historical_autonomist_and_secessionist_movements#British_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of historical autonomist and secessionist movements">Representative Government Association</a>. Marshaling public frustration with the lack of a voice in governing Dominica, this group won one-third of the popularly elected seats of the legislative assembly in 1924, and one-half in 1936. In 1940, administration of Dominica was transferred from the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a> to the <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, some Dominicans volunteered in British and Caribbean forces. Thousands of <a href="/wiki/Free_French" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French">Free French</a> refugees from Martinique and Guadeloupe escaped to Dominica from the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy</a>-controlled French islands, staying in <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> and other villages. </p>
      <p>Until 1958, Dominica was governed as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>. Caribbean islands sought independence from 1958 to 1962, and Dominica became a province of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> After the federation dissolved in 1962, Dominica became an associated state of the United Kingdom in 1967, and formally took responsibility for its internal affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> On 3 November 1978, the Commonwealth of Dominica was granted independence as a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Patrick_John" title="Patrick John">Patrick John</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence">Post-independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In mid-1979, political discontent with Founding Prime Minister Patrick John's administration climaxed in a civilian coup and ended in the passage of a Motion of No Confidence in the House of Assembly, Dominica's legislature, against John, collapsing the John administration. A new, so-called "Interim Government" was formed under Dominica's second Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Seraphin" title="Oliver Seraphin">Oliver Seraphin</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Seraphin's main task was to prepare the country for fresh general elections constitutionally due in 1980, hence the unofficial title "Interim" Prime Minister. Seraphin organized and led a splinter of the Dominica Labour Party called the Democratic Labour Party into the 1980 general election and lost mainly because his nearly thirteen month-long premiership was dominated by the fallout from Category Five <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a>, which caused 56 deaths and untold damage across the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tcr3_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcr3-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">Hurricane Allen</a> the following year caused further damage.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/1980_Dominican_general_election" title="1980 Dominican general election">1980 election</a>, Seraphin's government was replaced by one led by the <a href="/wiki/Dominica_Freedom_Party" title="Dominica Freedom Party">Dominica Freedom Party</a> (DFP) under Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Eugenia_Charles" title="Eugenia Charles">Eugenia Charles</a>; she was the Caribbean's first female Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1981, Charles's government was threatened with two attempted coups. The first was led by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Newton" title="Frederick Newton">Frederick Newton</a>, commander of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Dominica" title="Military of Dominica">Military of Dominica</a>, who organised an attack on the police headquarters in Roseau which resulted in the death of a police officer.<sup id="cite_ref-coup_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coup-28">[28]</a></sup> Newton and five other soldiers were found guilty in the attack and sentenced to death in 1983; the sentences of the five accomplices were later commuted to life in prison, but Newton was executed in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-coup_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coup-28">[28]</a></sup> A second occurred later in the year when the country was threatened with a takeover by <a href="/wiki/Mercenaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercenaries">mercenaries</a><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Red_Dog" title="Operation Red Dog">Operation Red Dog</a>, led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Perdue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mike Perdue (page does not exist)">Mike Perdue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Droege" title="Wolfgang Droege">Wolfgang Droege</a>. They tried to overthrow Charles as Prime Minister and reinstall ex-Prime Minister John in exchange for control over the country's development. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> was tipped off, and the ship hired to transport the mercenaries never left dock. The mercenaries lacked formal military experience or training, and most of the crew had been misled into joining by the ringleader Mike Perdue. <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">White supremacist</a> <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(white_nationalist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Don Black (white nationalist)">Don Black</a> was also jailed for his part in the attempted coup, which violated US <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_Act_of_1794" title="Neutrality Act of 1794">neutrality</a> laws.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg/220px-President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg/330px-President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg/440px-President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2647"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Ronald_Reagan_meets_with_Prime_Minister_Eugenia_Charles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Eugenia_Charles" title="Eugenia Charles">Eugenia Charles</a>, Prime Minister 1980–95, discussing the <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">situation in Grenada</a> in 1983 with US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Charles government supported the 1983 American <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">Invasion of Grenada</a>, earning Dominica praise from the Reagan administration and an increase in financial aid.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the middle of the 1980s, the economy had begun to recover,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> before weakening again due to a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> prices. Eugenia Charles won the <a href="/wiki/1985_Dominican_general_election" title="1985 Dominican general election">1985</a> general election, becoming only the first incumbent Dominica Prime Minister to be popularly re-elected. The continuing downturn in the economy and the tight grip by Eugenia Charles on Dominica politics gave rise to a self-titled "Third Force" political formation in 1988, which disrupted the traditional two-party arrangement of governing DFP and opposition DLP. "Third Force" soon formalized as United Workers Party and selected as its leader Edison James, the former General Manager of the Dominica Banana Marketing Company. This was a strategic selection given James's prestige among banana farmers and his originating from the East or Atlantic Coast that had begun to feel alienated by the West or Caribbean Sea Coast elites in Roseau, Dominica's capital.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> Eugenia Charles again won the <a href="/wiki/1990_Dominican_general_election" title="1990 Dominican general election">1990</a> general election, the first incumbent Dominica Prime Minister to win three consecutive general elections. However, Eugenia Charles's DFP had been pushed to within one seat of losing its majority in Parliament by the emergence of the UWP. It was, therefore, no great surprise when Eugenia Charles gave up political leadership of the Dominica Freedom Party in 1993 and did not contest the 1995 general election in any capacity. No longer benefiting from the veteran charismatic leadership of Prime Minister Eugenia Charles, the Dominica Freedom Party lost the <a href="/wiki/1995_Dominican_general_election" title="1995 Dominican general election">1995 election</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_Workers%27_Party_(Dominica)" title="United Workers' Party (Dominica)">United Workers' Party</a> (UWP), whose leader <a href="/wiki/Edison_James" title="Edison James">Edison James</a> became Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> James, former General Manager of the Dominica Banana Marketing Company attempted to diversify the Dominican economy away from over-reliance on bananas. The crop was largely destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Further James was unable to restore banana to its former selling price and prestige. Moreover, the James administration became embroiled in Opposition charges of official corruption. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2000_Dominican_general_election" title="2000 Dominican general election">31 January 2000 general election</a>, the UWP were defeated by a coalition of the DLP, led by left-leaning <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Douglas" title="Rosie Douglas">Roosevelt B. "Rosie" Douglas</a> and the Dominica Freedom Party led by former trade union leader, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Savarin" title="Charles Savarin">Charles Savarin</a>. Douglas became Prime Minister. One UWP member of the House of Assembly crossed the floor, joining the DLP-DFP coalition government. However, Douglas died on 1 October 2000 after only a few months.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Prime Minister Douglas was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Charles_(Dominican_politician)" title="Pierre Charles (Dominican politician)">Pierre Charles</a>, who also died in office on 6 January 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Skerrit" title="Roosevelt Skerrit">Roosevelt Skerrit</a>, also of the DLP, replaced Pierre Charles as Prime Minister, becoming the world's youngest head of government at thirty-one.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Under Skerrit's leadership, the DLP won <a href="/wiki/2005_Dominican_general_election" title="2005 Dominican general election">elections in May 2005</a> that gave the party 12 seats in the 21-seat Parliament, to the UWP's 8 seats. An independent candidate affiliated with the DLP won a seat as well. Later, the independent candidate joined the government.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> With his 2005 election win, Skerrit became only the second incumbent Prime Minister of seven to be popularly re-elected. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009_Dominican_general_election" title="2009 Dominican general election">2009 election</a>, the DLP won 18 of 21 seats. The UWP claimed campaign improprieties and embarked on a wide range of protest actions, including boycott of Parliament. UWP's boycott lasted at least three unauthorized absences from Parliament for two of their three Elected Representatives in Parliament in violation of Parliamentary procedure, leading to their two seats being declared vacant and by-elections being called to fill them; by-elections were conducted for those two vacant seats in July 2010, and the UWP again won both seats.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The DLP under Skerrit went on to win the <a href="/wiki/2014_Dominican_general_election" title="2014 Dominican general election">2014 Dominican general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CE_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 17 September 2012 <a href="/wiki/Eliud_Williams" title="Eliud Williams">Eliud Thaddeus Williams</a> was sworn in as President (a largely ceremonial role), replacing <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Liverpool" title="Nicholas Liverpool">Dr. Nicholas Liverpool</a> who was reportedly removed from office due to ill health. On 30 September 2013 former Trade Union leader and former Dominica Freedom Party leader Charles Savarin was elected president having only days before resigned as a Minister of Government. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_(37372721465).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg/220px-Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg/330px-Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg/440px-Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_%2837372721465%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5008" data-file-height="3336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_after_Hurricane_Maria_(37372721465).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Damage in <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> caused by Hurricane Maria in 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erika" title="Tropical Storm Erika">Tropical Storm Erika</a> devastated the island in August 2015, killing 30 and causing severe environmental and economic damage<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Dominica was again struck on 18 September 2017, suffering a direct landfall from Category 5 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Early estimates of damage suggested 90% of the buildings on the island had been destroyed, with infrastructure left in ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Handy_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handy-38">[38]</a></sup> The UK, France and the Netherlands set up shipping and air lifts to take aid to the island; the scale of destruction having left most people homeless. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RooseveltSkerrit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RooseveltSkerrit.jpg/170px-RooseveltSkerrit.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RooseveltSkerrit.jpg/255px-RooseveltSkerrit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RooseveltSkerrit.jpg/340px-RooseveltSkerrit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1050"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RooseveltSkerrit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The current Prime Minister of the Commonwealth of Dominica, Roosevelt Skerrit
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>. </p>
      <p>In December 2019, incumbent Prime Minister Roosevelt Skerrit won his fourth consecutive general election eighteen seats to three, becoming the first Dominica Prime Minister ever to do so. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg/220px-Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg/330px-Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg/440px-Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg 2x" data-file-width="838" data-file-height="1120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lesser_Antilles_250m.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dominica is an island in the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, located about halfway between the French islands of <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (to the north) and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> (to the south)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Dominica.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Map_of_Dominica.gif/220px-Map_of_Dominica.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Map_of_Dominica.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Dominica.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Dominica.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Dominica" title="Geography of Dominica">Geography of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Dominica is an <a href="/wiki/Island_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Island nation">island nation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the northernmost of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> (though it is sometimes considered the southernmost of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>). The size of the country is about 289.5 square miles (750&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) and it is about 29 miles (47&nbsp;km) long and 16 miles (26&nbsp;km) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Known as "The Nature Island of the Caribbean" due to its lush scenery and varied flora and fauna, Dominica is largely covered by <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> and is home to the world's second-largest <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot spring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boiling_Lake" title="Boiling Lake">Boiling Lake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Within its borders lie two ecoregions: Windward Islands moist forests and Windward Islands xeric scrub.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-42">[42]</a></sup> The most mountainous of the Lesser Antilles, its volcanic peaks are cones of lava craters, the largest of these being (north-to-south) <a href="/wiki/Morne_aux_Diables" title="Morne aux Diables">Morne aux Diables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morne_Diablotins" title="Morne Diablotins">Morne Diablotins</a> (the highest on the island at 1,447 m),<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Morne_Trois_Pitons" class="mw-redirect" title="Morne Trois Pitons">Morne Trois Pitons</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Morne_Anglais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Morne Anglais (page does not exist)">Morne Anglais</a>. <a href="/wiki/Morne_Trois_Pitons_National_Park" title="Morne Trois Pitons National Park">Morne Trois Pitons National Park</a> is a tropical forest blended with volcanic features;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> it was recognised as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> on 4 April 1995, a distinction it shares with four other Caribbean islands.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Calibishie" title="Calibishie">Calibishie</a> area in the country's northeast has sandy beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Some plants and animals thought to be extinct on surrounding islands can still be found in Dominica's forests.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The island has several <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected areas</a>, including <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Dominica" title="List of national parks of Dominica">Cabrits National Park</a>, as well as 365 rivers. For a few years the government sought to encourage the island as an <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> destination, although the hurricane of 2017 has since changed these plans.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> The country had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 1.06/10, ranking it 166th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are two primary population centres: the capital <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> (with 14,725 inhabitants in 2011) and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Dominica" title="Portsmouth, Dominica">Portsmouth</a> (with 4,167 inhabitants in 2011). The main centres tend to be located around the coast, with the mountainous interior sparsely populated.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dominica is especially vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">hurricanes</a> as the island is located in what is referred to as the hurricane region.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1979, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> struck the island as a Category&nbsp;4 hurricane, causing widespread and extreme damage. On 17 August 2007, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Hurricane Dean</a>, a Category&nbsp;1 hurricane at the time, hit the island. A mother and her seven-year-old son died when a <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslide</a> caused by the heavy rains crushed their house.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_Haiti_preps_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_Haiti_preps-48">[48]</a></sup> In another incident two people were injured when a tree fell on their house.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_2007-08-17_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc_2007-08-17-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Dominica" title="Prime Minister of Dominica">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Skerrit" title="Roosevelt Skerrit">Roosevelt Skerrit</a> estimated that 100 to 125 homes were damaged, and that the agricultural sector was extensively damaged, in particular the banana crop.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_2007-08-17_02_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc_2007-08-17_02-50">[50]</a></sup> In August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erika" title="Tropical Storm Erika">Tropical Storm Erika</a> caused extensive flooding and landslides across the island. Multiple communities were evacuated and upwards of 30 people were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> According to a Rapid Damage and Impact Assessment prepared for Dominica by the World Bank, the total damage and losses from the storm were US$484.82 million or 90% of Dominica's yearly GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Category 5 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck the island in 2017 and caused losses of approximately US$930 million or 226% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-Handy_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handy-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_amazon" title="Imperial amazon">Sisserou parrot</a> (<i>Amazona imperialis</i>) is Dominica's national bird and is <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to its mountain forests.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> A related species, the Jaco or <a href="/wiki/Red-necked_parrot" class="mw-redirect" title="Red-necked parrot">red-necked parrot</a> (<i>A. arausiaca</i>), is also a Dominican endemic.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> Both birds are rare and protected, though some forest is still threatened by logging in addition to the long-standing threat of hurricanes. </p>
      <p>Dominica has recorded at least four species of snakes and 11 species of lizards. </p>
      <p>Dominica is home to 195 species of birds, because of the isolated location of Dominica this is a lesser number compared to <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> which is located closer to mainland <a href="/wiki/South-America" class="mw-redirect" title="South-America">South-America</a> with 472 bird species. </p>
      <p>The Caribbean Sea offshore of the island of Dominica is home to many <a href="/wiki/Cetacean" class="mw-redirect" title="Cetacean">cetaceans</a>. Most notably a group of <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whales</a> live in this area year-round. Other cetaceans commonly seen in the area include <a href="/wiki/Spinner_dolphin" title="Spinner dolphin">spinner dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantropical_spotted_dolphin" title="Pantropical spotted dolphin">pantropical spotted dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphins</a>. Less commonly seen animals include <a href="/wiki/Killer_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Killer whales">killer whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/False_killer_whale" title="False killer whale">false killer whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_sperm_whale" title="Pygmy sperm whale">pygmy sperm whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_sperm_whale" title="Dwarf sperm whale">dwarf sperm whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Risso%27s_dolphin" title="Risso's dolphin">Risso's dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_spotted_dolphin" title="Atlantic spotted dolphin">Atlantic spotted dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Humpback whales">humpback whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale" title="Bryde's whale">Bryde's whales</a>. This makes Dominica a destination for tourists interested in <a href="/wiki/Whale-watching" class="mw-redirect" title="Whale-watching">whale-watching</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_disputes">Territorial disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Territorial disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Commonwealth of Dominica is engaged in a long-running dispute with <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> over Venezuela's territorial claims to the sea surrounding <a href="/wiki/Isla_Aves" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla Aves">Isla Aves</a> (literally Bird Island, but in fact called 'Bird Rock' by Dominican authorities),<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MitchellGold1983_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MitchellGold1983-53">[53]</a></sup> a tiny islet located 140 miles (225&nbsp;km) west of the island of Dominica. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Dominica" title="Politics of Dominica">Politics of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Dominica" title="Foreign relations of Dominica">Foreign relations of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Dominica is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-English_constitution_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_constitution-13">[13]</a></sup> The capital is <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a>. The Commonwealth of Dominica is one of the Caribbean's few <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a>. The president is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, while executive power rests with the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-English_constitution_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_constitution-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a> consists of the 30-member <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Dominica" title="House of Assembly of Dominica">House of Assembly</a>, which consists of 21 directly elected members and nine senators, who may either be appointed by the president or elected by the other members of the House of Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-English_constitution_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_constitution-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unlike other former British colonies in the region, Dominica was never a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, instead becoming a republic on independence. Dominica is a full and participating member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community (CARICOM)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dominica is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_Immunity_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral Immunity Agreement">Bilateral Immunity Agreement</a> of protection with the US military, as covered under <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Article 98</a>. In January 2008, Dominica joined the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alternative_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alternative for the Americas">Bolivarian Alternative for the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica_17-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Dominica-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Both male and female <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Dominica" title="LGBT rights in Dominica">same-sex sexual activity</a> is illegal in Dominica.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
