           <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:90px;top:400px">
            <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mark_Parish_(Dominica)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Mark Parish (Dominica)">Saint Mark</a>
           </div> 
           <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:40px;top:300px">
            <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea"><i>CARIBBEAN<br>SEA</i></a>
           </div> 
           <div style="position: absolute;font-size:100%;left:200px;top:30px">
            <a class="mw-selflink selflink"><i><b>DOMINICA</b></i></a>
           </div> 
          </div> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Dominica is divided into 10 <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Dominica" title="Parishes of Dominica">parishes</a>, given below with their 2011 Census populations: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Andrew Parish, Dominica">Saint Andrew Parish</a> (9,471)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_David_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint David Parish, Dominica">Saint David Parish</a> (6,043)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint George Parish, Dominica">Saint George Parish</a> (21,241)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_John_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint John Parish, Dominica">Saint John Parish</a> (6,561)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Joseph Parish, Dominica">Saint Joseph Parish</a> (5,637)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Luke_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Luke Parish, Dominica">Saint Luke Parish</a> (1,668)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Mark_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Mark Parish, Dominica">Saint Mark Parish</a> (1,834)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Patrick Parish, Dominica">Saint Patrick Parish</a> (7,622)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Paul Parish, Dominica">Saint Paul Parish</a> (9,786)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Peter Parish, Dominica">Saint Peter Parish</a> (1,430)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Dominica" title="Economy of Dominica">Economy of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="862"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Dominica.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Dominica's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Dominica's currency is the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="East Caribbean Dollar">East Caribbean Dollar</a>. In 2008, Dominica had one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) rates of Eastern Caribbean states.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The country nearly had a financial crisis in 2003 and 2004, but Dominica's economy grew by 3.5% in 2005 and 4.0% in 2006, following a decade of poor performance. Growth in 2006 was attributed to gains in tourism, construction, offshore and other services, and some sub-sectors of the banana industry. Around this time the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) praised the Government of Dominica for its successful macroeconomic reforms, but also pointed out remaining challenges, including the need for further reductions in public debt, increased financial sector regulation, and market diversification.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agriculture and especially bananas once dominated Dominica's economy,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> and nearly one-third of the labour force worked in agriculture in the early 2000s. This sector, however, is highly vulnerable to weather conditions and to external events affecting commodity prices. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Hurricane Dean</a> caused significant damage to the agricultural sector as well as the country's infrastructure, especially roads.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In response to reduced <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) <a href="/wiki/Trade_preference" title="Trade preference">trade preferences</a> for bananas from the former European colonies after the 2009 <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a> decision,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> the government has diversified the agricultural sector by promoting the production of coffee, <a href="/wiki/Patchouli" title="Patchouli">patchouli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aloe_vera" title="Aloe vera">aloe vera</a>, cut flowers, and exotic fruits such as mango, guava and papaya,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> while the economy has become increasingly dependent on tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica_39-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Dominica-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The expected increase of Dominica's <a href="/wiki/Immigrant_investor_programs" title="Immigrant investor programs">Citizenship by Investment</a> (CBI) fees has been suspended with no implementation date in sight, as announced by Prime Minister Roosevelt Skerrit, in the 2016 budget speech.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_trade">International trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: International trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica is a beneficiary of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin_Initiative" title="Caribbean Basin Initiative">Caribbean Basin Initiative</a> (CBI) that grants duty-free entry into the United States for many goods. Dominica also belongs to the predominantly English-speaking <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), the <a href="/wiki/CARICOM_Single_Market_and_Economy" title="CARICOM Single Market and Economy">CARICOM Single Market and Economy</a> (CSME), and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services_industry">Financial services industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Financial services industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Commonwealth of Dominica is becoming in recent years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2020)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> a major international financial centre. The largest sectors are "<a href="/wiki/Offshore_banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore banking">offshore banking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Payment_processing" class="mw-redirect" title="Payment processing">payment processing</a> companies, and general corporate activities". Regulation and supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> industry is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Service_Unit_of_the_Commonwealth_of_Dominica" title="Financial Service Unit of the Commonwealth of Dominica">Financial Service Unit of the Commonwealth of Dominica</a> (FSU) under the supervision of the Ministry of Finance. There are a number of service providers. These include global financial institutions including <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank" title="Scotiabank">Scotiabank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Canada" title="Royal Bank of Canada">Royal Bank of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Investment_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral Investment Bank">Cathedral Investment Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Caribbean_International_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="First Caribbean International Bank">First Caribbean International Bank</a>, and The Interoceanic Bank of the Caribbean. </p>
      <p>Starting in the mid-late 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centres" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore financial centres">offshore financial centres</a>, such as the Commonwealth of Dominica, came under increasing pressure from the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> for their allegedly harmful tax regimes, where the OECD wished to prevent low-tax regimes from having an advantage in the global marketplace. The OECD threatened to place the Commonwealth of Dominica and other <a href="/wiki/Financial_centres" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial centres">financial centres</a> on a "black list" and impose sanctions against them. However, the Commonwealth of Dominica successfully avoided being placed on the OECD black list by committing to regulatory reform to improve transparency and begin information exchange with OECD member countries about their citizens. </p>
      <p>Dominica supposedly offers tax-free status to companies relocating from abroad. It is not known how many companies benefit from the tax-free status because of the strict confidentiality the government enforces, although it is known many <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> businesses and <a href="/wiki/Hedge_fund" title="Hedge fund">hedge funds</a> utilise Dominica for this reason. However, on 12 July 2012 Dominica signed an agreement with Poland to exchange tax information.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_immigrants">Economic immigrants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economic immigrants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dominica_citizenship_by_investment_programme" title="Dominica citizenship by investment programme">Dominica citizenship by investment programme</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Commonwealth of Dominica offers an official and legally mandated <a href="/wiki/Economic_citizenship" title="Economic citizenship">economic citizenship</a> to those seeking a valid second citizenship. The nationality law of Dominica authorises the government to waive the normal requirement of seven years of legal residence to acquire citizenship in exchange for an investment into their country's economy. The required contribution for a main applicant starts at US$100,000 through the Economic Diversification Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Alternatively, since 2014, applicants can make a US$200,000 minimum investment in pre-approved real estate from island exclusive resorts or global brands like Marriott, Kempinski or Hilton.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> According to officials, the <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_by_investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizenship by investment">citizenship by investment</a> (CBI) programme was an economic and fiscal "lifeline" in the aftermath of Tropical Storm Erika in 2015 and Hurricane Maria in 2017, and its new investment option had become the main source of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Direct_Investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Direct Investment">Foreign Direct Investment</a> into Dominica by early 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Dominican citizens can travel without a visa, or obtain a visa upon entry, to nearly 140 countries and territories, including the United Kingdom and the Schengen Zone.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Applying for Dominica citizenship requires interacting with official Government Approved Economic Citizenship Agents as the first step in the application process.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> This program is currently valued at 16% of the government's total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government's management of the economic citizenship programme and an initial perceived lack of transparency in the use of the revenues generated are a frequent topic of heated domestic political controversy. Referring to the opposition, Prime Minister Skerrit in 2016 stated that "If they can discredit the Citizenship by Investment Program and make Dominica an unattractive place to obtain citizenship, then revenues would fall and the government would not be able to rebuild the country. Or, the government would then have to increase taxes on the people; making itself unpopular in their sight."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Since then, the Government of Dominica has improved transparency of CBI funds. According to Prime Minister Skerrit's 2018-2019 Budget Address,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> the island's CBI Programme has helped develop a National Health Insurance pilot that provides Dominican children in critical medical conditions with overseas treatment. Because many residents were displaced by Hurricane Maria's impact on the small Caribbean island, the government pledged to build 5,000 hurricane-proof homes, of which the first batch of 125 houses were scheduled for occupancy in February 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The CBI Programme has also significantly helped to develop and create jobs in the island's ecotourism sector.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Furthermore, the Skerrit administration set aside EC$5m every month for the construction of a new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a>' Professional Wealth Management publication ranked Dominica as the world's best citizenship by investment programme in its annual CBI Index.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> According to the report, investors choose Dominica's citizenship because it has the most affordable investment threshold, the application process is straightforward and streamlined,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> while the security checks each applicant is subjected to remain very strict.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Batalie_Bay,_Dominica_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg/220px-Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg/330px-Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg/440px-Batalie_Bay%2C_Dominica_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3996" data-file-height="2697"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Batalie_Bay,_Dominica_002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Batalie Bay, Dominica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica is mostly volcanic and has few beaches; therefore, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Dominica" title="Tourism in Dominica">tourism</a> has developed more slowly than on neighbouring islands. Nevertheless, Dominica's mountains, rainforests, freshwater lakes, hot springs, waterfalls, and diving spots make it an attractive <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> destination. Cruise ship stopovers have increased following the development of modern docking and waterfront facilities in Roseau, the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_19-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-19">[19]</a></sup> Out of 22 Caribbean islands tracked, Dominica had the fewest visitors in 2008 (55,800 or 0.3% of the total). This was about half as many as visited Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The volcanic nature of the island has attracted <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba divers</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are two regional airports on the island, but no international airports. Therefore, flying to Dominica requires travelling through <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a> or other nearby islands in the Caribbean such as <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>. The primary airport, <a href="/wiki/Douglas-Charles_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas-Charles Airport">Douglas-Charles Airport</a> (DOM), is on the northeast coast and is about a 45-minute drive from Portsmouth (1 hour from Roseau). The second is <a href="/wiki/Canefield_Airport" title="Canefield Airport">Canefield Airport</a> (DCF), about 15 minutes from Roseau on the southwest coast. Douglas-Charles Airport is suitable for limited use of commercial jets because of runway length. Douglas-Charles currently has regular service by <a href="/wiki/Air_Sunshine" title="Air Sunshine">Air Sunshine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winair" title="Winair">Winair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seaborne_Airlines" title="Seaborne Airlines">Seaborne Airlines</a> using twin turboprop aircraft like the <a href="/wiki/ATR_(aircraft_manufacturer)" title="ATR (aircraft manufacturer)">ATR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saab_340" title="Saab 340">Saab 340</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Conviasa" title="Conviasa">Conviasa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amerijet" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerijet">Amerijet</a>, which, using <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727 Freighters</a>, is the only airline with jet service to the republic. A runway extension and service upgrade project began at Douglas-Charles Airport around 2006 and was finished in 2010. In March 2013, airline American Eagle halted flights to the island citing high labour costs.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Petite_Savanne,_Dominica,_after_Tropical_Storm_Erika.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5f/Petite_Savanne%2C_Dominica%2C_after_Tropical_Storm_Erika.jpg/280px-Petite_Savanne%2C_Dominica%2C_after_Tropical_Storm_Erika.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/5f/Petite_Savanne%2C_Dominica%2C_after_Tropical_Storm_Erika.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="386" data-file-height="257"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Petite_Savanne,_Dominica,_after_Tropical_Storm_Erika.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Petite Savanne <i>(pictured)</i> was uninhabitable after numerous landslides.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica's road network runs primarily along the coastline and along river valleys. Major roads are two-lane highways which connect the capital, Roseau, with Portsmouth (<a href="/wiki/Edward_Oliver_LeBlanc" title="Edward Oliver LeBlanc">Edward Oliver Leblanc Highway</a>) and the Douglas Charles Airport (Dr. Nicholas Liverpool Highway). It takes about 45 minutes to drive from Portsmouth to Roseau. Private minibuses form the major public transport system. These major roads were reconstructed from the early 2010s to 2015 with assistance from the People's Republic of China and the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erika#Effects_in_Dominica" title="Tropical Storm Erika">Tropical Storm Erika of 2015</a> several road surfaces and bridges were damaged by flooding and landslides, including on the just completed E.O. LeBlanc Highway (Roseau to Portsmouth) and <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Liverpool" title="Nicholas Liverpool">Dr. Nicholas Liverpool Highway</a> (Pont Cassé to Douglas Charles Airport). To alleviate this, the government announced that it intended to install emergency bridges in Roseau Valley near the Trafalgar Falls to Wotten Waven and in Emshall.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria#Dominica" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria of 2017</a> also damaged the road network. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_energy">Green energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Green energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Dominica's electricity sector includes power from hydroelectricity, solar energy, and geothermal energy.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Following on from the devastation caused by Hurricane Maria in September 2017, the Dominican government claimed it would invest in geothermal energy. In early March 2018 Dominica signed an <a href="/wiki/International_Solar_Alliance" title="International Solar Alliance">International Solar Alliance</a> Framework Agreement, in an attempt to exploit solar energy to power the country with a source of renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Dominica" title="Demographics of Dominica">Demographics of Dominica</a>
      </div>

       <caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa solid;background-color:lavender;padding:0.25em;font-weight:bold">
        Dominica
       </caption>

         <td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup id="cite_ref-2011_census_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_census-6">[6]</a></sup></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The vast majority of Dominicans are of African descent. There is a growing mixed population along with a small European origin minority (descendants of French and British colonists along with some people of Irish descent from indentured servants) and there are small numbers of Lebanese, Syrians and Asians. Dominica is also the only Eastern Caribbean island that still has a population of pre-Columbian native <a href="/wiki/Kalinago" title="Kalinago">Kalinago</a> (previously called Caribs), who were exterminated or driven from neighbouring islands. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are more than 3,000 Kalinago remaining. They live in eight villages on the east coast of Dominica. This special <a href="/wiki/Carib_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Carib Territory">Carib Territory</a> (now Kalinago Territory) was granted by the British Crown in 1903.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Scotts_Head,_Dominica_021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg/220px-Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg/330px-Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg/440px-Scotts_Head%2C_Dominica_021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Scotts_Head,_Dominica_021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Scotts Head, Dominica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population growth rate of Dominica is very low, due primarily to emigration to other countries. In the early 21st century, emigrant numbers for the most popular countries are as follows: the United States (8,560), the United Kingdom (6,739), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (605), and France (394). </p>
      <p>Dominica had a relatively large number of <a href="/wiki/Centenarian" title="Centenarian">centenarians</a>. In March 2007 there were 22 centenarians out of the island's 70,000 inhabitants —three times the average incidence of centenarianism in developed countries. The reasons for this were once the subject of a study that formerly had been undertaken at <a href="/wiki/Ross_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Ross University School of Medicine">Ross University School of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOC_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOC-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dominica was partially integrated into the federal colony of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> in 1832. Later, in 1871, it became a full part of the Federation of the Leeward Islands. From the start it was a peculiar relationship for previously Dominica had played no part in the political or cultural traditions of the other more Anglophone islands of the federation. Now, as a Leeward Island, this much larger territory, with thousands of acres of forested unclaimed land, was open to the people of <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. At the beginning of the 20th century, the Rose's Company, which produced <a href="/wiki/Rose%27s_lime_juice" title="Rose's lime juice">Rose's lime juice</a>, saw demand for its product outgrow its ability to supply the product from Montserrat. Their response to the situation was to buy land on Dominica and encourage Montserrat farm labourers to relocate. As a result, there came to be two linguistic communities in Dominica, <a href="/wiki/Wesley,_Dominica" title="Wesley, Dominica">Wesley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marigot,_Dominica" title="Marigot, Dominica">Marigot</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roseau_-_Charlotteville_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Charlotteville, Dominica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1902, on 8 May, the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pel%C3%A9e" title="Mount Pelée">Mount Pelée</a> volcano on Martinique erupted destroying the city of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre,_Martinique" title="Saint-Pierre, Martinique">Saint-Pierre</a>. Refugees from Martinique arrived in boats to the southern villages of Dominica and some remained permanently on the island. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is the official language of Dominica and is universally spoken and understood. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominican Creole">Dominican Creole</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a> based on <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, is widely spoken. This is due to French migration to the island starting in 1690, a majority French Creole speaking population that resided on the island,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and its location between the two French-speaking departments of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>. Since 1979, Dominica has been a member of <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. Dominican Creole is particularly used among the older generation, which also speaks a <a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">patois</a> language. Because of a decline in the use of Creole by the younger generation, initiatives have been set up in an effort to increase usage and promote this unique part of the nation's history and culture. </p>
      <p>Along with Creole, a dialect known as Kokoy (or Cockoy) is spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> It is a type of <a href="/wiki/List_of_English-based_pidgins" title="List of English-based pidgins">pidgin English</a> which is a mix of Leeward Island <a href="/wiki/English_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="English Creole">English Creole</a> and Dominican Creole,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and is mainly spoken in the north-eastern villages of Marigot and Wesley, by the descendants of immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. Over time there has been much intermarrying, but there are still traces of difference in origin.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> As a result of this mixture of languages and heritage, Dominica is a member of both the French-speaking Francophonie and the English-speaking <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Island_Carib_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Carib language">Island Carib</a>, also known as Igneri (Iñeri, Igñeri, Inyeri), was an <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawakan language">Arawakan language</a> historically spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. The Island Caribs lived throughout the southern Lesser Antilles such as Dominica, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">St Vincent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad</a>, supposedly having conquered them from their previous inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Igneri" title="Igneri">Igneri</a>. Island Carib became extinct about 1920, but an offshoot survives as <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_language" title="Garifuna language">Garifuna</a>, primarily in Central America. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Dominica" title="Religion in Dominica">Religion in Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roseau_Virgin_Ln_-_Our_Lady_of_Fair_Haven_Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Roseau_Cathedral" title="Roseau Cathedral">Roseau Cathedral</a> in Dominica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>61.4% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> though in recent years a number of <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches have been established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> About 10–12% of the population belongs to one of the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_theology" title="Seventh-day Adventist theology">Seventh-Day</a> (Saturday) denominations, which includes Yahweh Congregation, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Seventh-Day)" title="Church of God (Seventh-Day)">Church of God (Seventh-Day)</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a>, in 2010 the World Christian Database reported that the largest non-Christian religious groups included: <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">spiritualism</a> followed by 2.6% of the population; <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a> followed by 1.7%; <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">Agnosticism</a> followed by 0.5%; <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, each followed by 0.1%; and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neoreligion" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoreligion">Neoreligions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheism</a> each followed by non-negligible proportions (i.e., &lt;0.1%) of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The nation's first <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> was built near Ross University.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Dominica" title="Education in Dominica">Education in Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>School in Dominica is mandatory up to secondary school. After pre-school, pupils attend primary school for six or seven years, and are admitted into secondary school on the basis of a Common Entrance Exam. After five years the students take the General Certificate of Education (GCE), widely replaced by the current Caribbean Secondary Education Certificate administered by the Caribbean Examination Council (a 15-member confederation of the Caribbean community (CARICOM). The more advanced version of this examination, CAPE, can be taken upon completion of two years of community college. The island has its own <a href="/wiki/Dominica_State_College" title="Dominica State College">Dominica State College</a>, formerly named Clifton Dupigny Community College. Some Dominicans attend universities in Cuba on scholarships offered by its government; others go to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> or to universities in the United Kingdom, the United States, or other countries. </p>
      <p>Archbold Tropical Research and Education Center, a biological field station owned by <a href="/wiki/Clemson_University" title="Clemson University">Clemson University</a>, is located at Springfield Estate between <a href="/wiki/Canefield" title="Canefield">Canefield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pont_Cass%C3%A9" title="Pont Cassé">Pont Cassé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2006 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.allsaintsuniversity.org/">All Saints University School of Medicine</a> opened in temporary facilities in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Loubi%C3%A8re&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Loubière (page does not exist)">Loubière</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> it was later located in <a href="/wiki/Roseau,_Dominica" class="mw-redirect" title="Roseau, Dominica">Roseau, Dominica</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">marine biology</a> institute in <a href="/wiki/Mahaut,_Dominica" title="Mahaut, Dominica">Mahaut</a>, the Institute for Tropical Marine Ecology, closed in 2009. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ross_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Ross University School of Medicine">Ross University School of Medicine</a> was located at <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Dominica" title="Portsmouth, Dominica">Portsmouth</a>. Ross had been operating in Dominica since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> There used to be a thousand medical students arriving annually from the United States and Canada who studied at Ross University, but the campus was permanently relocated to <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> at the beginning of the 2019 Spring semester due to extensive hurricane damage suffered at the Dominican campus.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Dominica Library and Information Service serves an integral role in the education of the citizens of the country. The creation of a public library in Dominica did not come easily though the impetus was a noble one that would help "the coloured people... [improve] their lot as they moved along the path to complete freedom...” (Boromé, 203). The Dominican library began as a reading room that would evolve into a free and public library that wasn't fully free: patrons were required to pay a subscription fee. Surviving religious and political discord, the great depression, and two world wars, the library finally came under the care of the government where funds were set aside for its upkeep. Ironically, the early stages of the library's history were dedicated to remove the "uncouth", and "barbarous patois", which today is being preserved. However, it did achieve its goal of "diminishing the island’s very high percentage of illiteracy" (pg. 225).<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> However, the historical library was demolished in the wake on hurricane Maria in 2018, and slated to be rebuilt with a more modern outlook. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Dominica" title="Culture of Dominica">Culture of Dominica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Dominica" title="Music of Dominica">Music of Dominica</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carib_Territory.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Carib_Territory.svg/220px-Carib_Territory.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Carib_Territory.svg/330px-Carib_Territory.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Carib_Territory.svg/440px-Carib_Territory.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1189"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carib_Territory.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dominica's east coast <a href="/wiki/Carib_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Carib Territory">Carib Territory</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Dominica is home to a wide range of people. Although it was historically occupied by several native tribes, the <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawaks</a> (Tainos) and Carib (Kalinago) tribes occupied it at the time European settlers reached the island. "<a href="/wiki/Massacre_River_(Dominica)" title="Massacre River (Dominica)">Massacre</a>" is a name of a river dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Kalinago_Genocide_of_1626" title="Kalinago Genocide of 1626">mass murder of the native villagers</a> by English settlers on St. Kitts -the survivors were forced into exile on Dominica.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-103">[103]</a></sup> Both the French and British tried to claim the island and imported <a href="/wiki/Slaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Slaves">slaves</a> from Africa for labour. The remaining Caribs now live on a 3,700-acre (15&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) territory on the east coast of the island. They elect their own chief. This mix of cultures has produced the current culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (February 2021)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Music and dance are important facets of Dominica's culture. The annual independence celebrations display a variety of traditional song and dance. Since 1997, there have also been weeks of Creole festivals, such as "Creole in the Park" and the "<a href="/wiki/World_Creole_Music_Festival" title="World Creole Music Festival">World Creole Music Festival</a>". </p>
      <p>Dominica gained prominence on the international music stage when in 1973, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Henderson_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gordon Henderson (musician)">Gordon Henderson</a> founded the group <a href="/wiki/Exile_One" title="Exile One">Exile One</a> and an original musical genre, which he coined "<a href="/wiki/Cadence-lypso" title="Cadence-lypso">Cadence-lypso</a>". This paved the way for modern Creole music. Other musical genres include "<a href="/wiki/Jing_ping" title="Jing ping">Jing ping</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Cadence_rampa" title="Cadence rampa">Cadence</a>". Jing ping features the accordion and is native to the island. Dominica's music is a mélange of Haitian, Afro-Cuban, African and European traditions. Popular artists over the years include Chubby and the Midnight Groovers, Bells Combo, the Gaylords, <a href="/wiki/Windward_Caribbean_Kulture" title="Windward Caribbean Kulture">WCK</a>, and Triple Kay. </p>
      <p>The 11th annual World <a href="/wiki/Creole_music" title="Creole music">Creole Music</a> Festival was held in 2007, part of the island's celebration of independence from Great Britain on 3 November. A year-long reunion celebration began in January 2008, marking 30 years of independence. </p>
      <p>Dominica is often seen as a society that is migrating from <a href="/wiki/Collectivism" title="Collectivism">collectivism</a> to that of individualism. The economy is a developing one that previously depended on agriculture. Signs of collectivism are evident in the small towns and villages which are spread across the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2020)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The novelist <a href="/wiki/Jean_Rhys" title="Jean Rhys">Jean Rhys</a> was born and raised in Dominica. The island is obliquely depicted in her best-known book, <i><a href="/wiki/Wide_Sargasso_Sea" title="Wide Sargasso Sea">Wide Sargasso Sea</a></i>. Rhys's friend, the political activist and writer <a href="/wiki/Phyllis_Shand_Allfrey" title="Phyllis Shand Allfrey">Phyllis Shand Allfrey</a>, set her 1954 novel, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orchid_House_(novel)" title="The Orchid House (novel)">The Orchid House</a></i>, in Dominica. </p>
      <p>Much of the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest</a></i> (the second in the series, released in 2006), was shot on location on Dominica (though in the film it was known as "Pelegosto", a fictional island), along with some shooting for the third film in the series, <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">At World's End</a></i> (2007). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dominica_cuisine" title="Dominica cuisine">Dominica cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Dominica's cuisine is similar to that of other Caribbean islands, particularly Jamaica, Saint Lucia and Trinidad and Tobago. Like other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Caribbean" title="Commonwealth Caribbean">Commonwealth Caribbean</a> islands, Dominicans have developed a distinct twist to their cuisine. Breakfast is an important daily meal, typically including saltfish, dried and salted <a href="/wiki/Codfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Codfish">codfish</a>, and "bakes" (fried dough). Saltfish and bakes are combined for a fast food snack that can be eaten throughout the day; vendors on Dominica's streets sell these snacks to passersby, together with fried chicken, fish and fruit and yogurt "smoothies". Other breakfast meals include cornmeal <a href="/wiki/Porridge" title="Porridge">porridge</a>, which is made with fine cornmeal or <i>polenta</i>, milk or condensed milk, and sugar to sweeten. Traditional British-influenced dishes, such as eggs, bacon and toast, are also popular, as are fried fish and <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>. </p>
      <p>Common vegetables include <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, tanias (a root vegetable), <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Potatoes">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_and_peas" title="Rice and peas">rice and peas</a>. Meat and poultry typically eaten include chicken, beef and fish. These are often prepared in stews with onions, carrots, garlic, ginger and herbs. The vegetables and meat are browned to create a rich dark sauce. Popular meals include rice and peas, <a href="/wiki/Brown_stew_chicken" title="Brown stew chicken">brown stew chicken</a>, stew beef, fried and stewed fish, and many different types of hearty fish broths and soups. These are filled with dumplings, carrots and ground provisions. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is a popular sport on the island, and Dominica competes in <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">test cricket</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>. In West Indies domestic first-class cricket, Dominica participates as part of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Windward Islands cricket team">Windward Islands cricket team</a>, although they are often considered a part of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> geographically. This is due to being part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a> colony from 1940 until independence; its cricket federation remains a part of the Windward Islands Cricket Board of Control. </p>
      <p>On 24 October 2007, the 8,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Park_(Dominica)" title="Windsor Park (Dominica)">Windsor cricket stadium</a> was completed with a donation of <a href="/wiki/EC$" class="mw-redirect" title="EC$">EC$</a>33&nbsp;million (<a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>17&nbsp;million, <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>12&nbsp;million) from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the People's Republic of China">government of the People's Republic of China</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">Netball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> are gaining popularity as well. </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>, a husband and wife team of Gary di Silvestri and Angela Morrone di Silvestri spent <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>175,000 to register as Dominican citizens and enter the 15&nbsp;km men's and 10&nbsp;km women's <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_at_the_2014_Winter_Olympics" title="Cross-country skiing at the 2014 Winter Olympics">cross-country skiing</a> events, respectively. Angela did not start her race, and Gary pulled out several hundred meters into his race. To date, they are Dominica's only Winter Olympic athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Athlete <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Romain" title="Jérôme Romain">Jérôme Romain</a> won the bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics">1995 World Championships in Athletics</a> <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_triple_jump" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics – Men's triple jump">triple jump competition</a>. He also qualified for the finals at the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_triple_jump" title="Athletics at the 1996 Summer Olympics – Men's triple jump">1996 Olympic Games</a>; even though he had to pull out due to injury, his 12th position is the best performance of a Dominican ever at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympics</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Dominica has two major newspapers, <i>The Sun</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronicle_(Dominica)" title="The Chronicle (Dominica)">The Chronicle</a></i>. There are two national television stations and a few radio stations, including Stations include: ZBC-AM 590, the first private local radio station is called Radio En Ba Mango 93.5/96.9FM in the Village of Berricoa Grand Bay and is owned by Urban Dangleben, ZGBC-AM 740, ZGBC-FM 90.7 (Portsmouth), ZGBC-FM 102.1 (Roseau) and ZGBC-FM 106.1 (Marigot), Q95 FM,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dominica_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Dominica Broadcasting Corporation">Dominica Broadcasting Corporation</a>, and Kairi FM.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Before 2004, there were two telecommunication companies <a href="/wiki/Cable_and_Wireless_(Caribbean)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cable and Wireless (Caribbean)">Cable and Wireless</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marpin_TV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marpin TV (page does not exist)">Marpin TV</a><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> founded by Dominican, Ronald Bernard Maroni Abraham. In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a> and a UK-based company <a href="/wiki/Orange_SA" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange SA">Orange</a> started to offer service to the island. There are a number of mobile networks operating on the island; LIME and Digicel compete for most of Dominica's wireless customers. Orange shut down in 2010 and is no longer operating on the island of Dominica. </p>
      <p>Historical newspapers include <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dloc.com/AA00079438/00001"><i>The Dominican</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dloc.com/AA00079437/00003/allvolumes"><i>The Dominica Guardian</i></a>, and the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dloc.com/AA00079447/00564/allvolumes"><i>Dominica Colonist</i></a>, available for free in the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Library_of_the_Caribbean" title="Digital Library of the Caribbean">Digital Library of the Caribbean</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
